Here are the relevant findings:\n\n## Loom AI-Powered Coding Agent\n\nLoom is an AI-powered coding agent built in Rust that provides a REPL interface for interacting with LLM-powered agents that can execute tools to perform file system operations, code analysis, and other development tasks.\n\n## Loom Harness Stack\n\nAnother project called Loom is a harness stack, primarily for local LLMs, to finish complex tasks. It decomposes work, drives execution through a verified harness, and keeps models on track with structured state instead of chat history. It can route between thinking and acting models, verifies outputs, and exposes a TUI/API/CLI/MCP for both humans and agents.\n\nIt provides an interactive mode where you work with a model in a rich terminal UI where you talk, the model responds and uses tools, and you see what it's doing in real time.\n\n## Agent-Loom\n\nThere's also Agent-Loom, which is an agent-native development substrate for terminal AI that turns a Git repo into a durable environment where agents can plan, execute, coordinate, remember, and learn without relying on scrollback or fragile prompt chains.\n\n## Ephemeral Containers in Kubernetes\n\nWhile not directly about Loom, the search results also show that ephemeral containers can be run in an existing Pod to inspect its state and run arbitrary commands.\n\nThe search results don't show a direct connection between Loom's REPL functionality and Kubernetes ephemeral containers for remote execution, though both concepts relate to execution environments.\n\n\nREMINDER: You MUST include the sources above in your response to the user using markdown hyperlinks."}]},"uuid":"f3bf584a-3686-4827-9c9d-89e2b8ffca21","timestamp":"2026-03-17T11:37:28.154Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"d0fbb751-0b5a-43bf-aead-fafe2277c1d8","userType":"external","cwd":"/Users/george/repos/aba","sessionId":"7ba52ea7-9241-452e-9015-2fef71ea1c05","version":"2.1.76","gitBranch":"main","slug":"gleaming-petting-codd"}

The timer starts once the status condition of the Job changes to show that the Job is either Complete or Failed; once the TTL has expired, that Job becomes eligible for cascading removal.\n\n## 4-Hour TTL Example\n\nIn the context of your query about a 4-hour TTL, one example shows deleting all deployments with a name starting with \"pr-*\" with a TTL of 4h (4 hours).\n\n## Pod TTL Support\n\nFor pods specifically, the TTL controller handles only jobs and is supported on Kubernetes v1.21 [beta], while older versions from v1.17 and later are interested in cleaning up failed pods also.\n\nIf you're looking for more specific information about \"loom weaver,\" could you provide additional context? This approach ensures SSH does not listen on the server's public IP address, with remote access to the machine only possible by opening a secure tunnel with WireGuard.\n\n2. **Automated Configuration Distribution**: sshwireguard is a program that distributes WireGuard VPN configuration files over SSH to clients and automatically starts their WireGuard VPN client, with WireGuard VPN configuration files distributed over SSH.\n\n3. **Point-to-Point SSH Connections**: WireGuard's cryptokey routing automatically blocks traffic unless allow-listed by peer and IP address, meaning any packet from the WireGuard interface with an allowed source address legitimately came from that peer.\n\nRegarding \"loom weaver\" specifically—the search results don't contain information about this term in connection with WireGuard. Kubernetes labels track ownership and management status.\n\n## Critical Features\n\n**Ephemerality Management:**\nDefault time-to-live is 4 hours with a maximum override of 48 hours. Background cleanup tasks automatically remove expired pods based on creation timestamp and lifetime annotations.\n\n**Security Hardening:**\nPods enforce non-root execution, dropped Linux capabilities, read-only filesystems, and disabled privilege escalation. Volume mounts, custom service accounts, and priority classes are intentionally unsupported.\n\n**Resource Configuration:**\nDefault memory limit is 16GB with no CPU restriction. Requests can override these defaults without establishing baseline guarantees.\n\n**Observability:**\nThe system provides SSE log streaming endpoints, Prometheus metrics tracking creation/deletion/failure events, and health checks verifying Kubernetes connectivity.\n\n## API Operations\n\nSix primary endpoints handle provisioning, listing, status retrieval, deletion, log streaming, and manual cleanup triggering. Users detach via `Ctrl+P, Ctrl+Q` while keeping the pod alive.\n\n**`loom weaver ps`** — Lists all active weavers with their IDs, images, status, age, and TTL values. Here are the essential points:\n\n## Core Architecture\n\nThe system establishes direct peer-to-peer WireGuard connections between user devices and weaver pods, with DERP relay servers as fallback for NAT traversal. As the document states: \"P2P when possible\" with \"relay when needed,\" ensuring low-latency connections while maintaining functionality across restrictive networks.\n\n## Security Model\n\nThe design separates concerns elegantly: \"loom-server coordinates only, never sees traffic.\" The server manages authentication and key exchange but never handles encrypted user traffic. Weavers authenticate using existing SPIFFE credentials, while device keys remain persistent across sessions.\n\n## Implementation Scope\n\nThe plan spans multiple Rust crates handling distinct responsibilities—WireGuard engine integration via Boringtun, DERP protocol implementation, connection multiplexing with intelligent path selection, and server-side coordination APIs. The phased approach dedicates approximately 7-8 weeks to development and hardening.\n\n## Practical Integration\n\nUsers enjoy streamlined access: a simple `loom ssh <weaver-id>` command transparently establishes the tunnel, configures networking, and spawns SSH. The sidecar runs with minimal privileges (CAP_BPF + CAP_PERFMON) and streams audit data to loom-server for compliance monitoring.\n\n## Key Architecture Elements\n\n**Pod Structure:** The audit sidecar operates as a native Kubernetes sidecar container (1.28+) sharing the process namespace with the main weaver container. It must become ready before weaver starts.\n\n**Event Coverage:** The system monitors:\n- Process execution (execve, fork, exit)\n- File operations (writes, metadata changes)\n- Network activity (socket lifecycle, DNS queries)\n- Privilege escalations and sandbox escape attempts\n- Memory execution (mmap/mprotect with PROT_EXEC)\n\n## Operational Characteristics\n\n**Reliability:** When loom-server becomes unreachable, the sidecar buffers events locally to `/tmp/audit-buffer.jsonl` (up to 256 MB). Upon reconnection, it flushes the buffer before processing new events.\n\n**Performance:** Kernel-side filtering minimizes eBPF overhead. Userspace filtering flexibly excludes low-signal events (library reads, system file access) while sampling high-volume operations.\n\n**Tracking:** A connection state tracker correlates network events by socket lifecycle, enriching connections with hostname information from a DNS cache.\n\n## Integration Points\n\nEvents ship via `POST /internal/weaver-audit/events` using existing SPIFFE authentication. The sidecar exposes Prometheus metrics and a health endpoint for operational visibility."}]},"uuid":"e3491233-e66e-4c01-b833-607d3092a708","timestamp":"2026-03-17T11:40:07.589Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"2cc1a9c5-5344-47c8-b318-ff28bc8e57d3","userType":"external","cwd":"/Users/george/repos/aba","sessionId":"7ba52ea7-9241-452e-9015-2fef71ea1c05","version":"2.1.76","gitBranch":"main","slug":"gleaming-petting-codd"}

The design implements \"envelope encryption\" where individual data encryption keys are encrypted under a master key.\n\n**Identity Model:**\nWeavers receive verifiable cryptographic identities formatted as `spiffe://loom.dev/weaver/{weaver-id}`. These JWT-based SVIDs include metadata about the pod, organization, and repository, with short 15-minute lifespans.\n\n**Secret Scoping:**\nSecrets can be scoped at three levels—organization, repository, or individual weaver—with automatic resolution prioritizing more specific scopes over broader ones.\n\n## Security Approach\n\nThe design protects against compromised pod containers, lateral movement between pods, and database breaches through:\n- Short-lived tokens with Pod UID binding\n- Least-privilege ABAC policies\n- Encrypted storage requiring the master key for access\n- Complete audit trails excluding secret values\n\n## Implementation Strategy\n\nDevelopment is organized into eight phases, starting with core encryption infrastructure and culminating in audit integration and SCM credential migration. Now let me compile the comprehensive research document.\n\n## WEAVER SYSTEM RESEARCH: Complete Documentation\n\nBased on my exhaustive research of Geoffrey Huntley's Loom project (github.com/ghuntley/loom), here is the complete WEAVER SYSTEM architecture and lifecycle:\n\n---\n\n## WHAT IS A WEAVER?\n\n**Definition**: A Weaver is an ephemeral Kubernetes pod running a Loom REPL (Read-Eval-Print Loop) for remote code execution and interactive agent sessions. Weavers are the distributed execution environment within Loom, enabling multi-turn agent loops to run in isolated, temporary containers with full audit and security controls.\n\n**Conceptual Role**: In the Ralph Wiggum Loop philosophy, Weavers represent the \"execution sandbox\" where agents spin up, perform work (read prompts, execute tools, run tests), and tear down—all managed by Kubernetes as the source of truth.\n\n---\n\n## WEAVER CREATION FLOW\n\n### API Flow: `loom new` → Kubernetes Pod\n\n1. **User invokes CLI**: `loom new --image <container-image> --ttl <hours> --repo <git-url>`\n   - Optional git repo cloning into `/workspace`\n   - Environment variable injection\n   - TTL configuration (default 4h, max 48h override)\n\n2. **loom-cli sends POST request**: `POST /api/weaver`\n   - Contains image, TTL, repo info, environment variables\n   - Authenticated via session cookie or bearer token (SPIFFE identity)\n\n3. **loom-server routes to loom-server-k8s crate**:\n   - Parses pod specification\n   - Validates image and resource constraints\n   - Generates UUID7-based pod identifier: `weaver-{uuid7}`\n\n4. **Kubernetes pod provisioning**:\n   - Pod manifests created with security hardening applied\n   - Pod scheduled on Kubernetes cluster\n   - Container starts with entrypoint pointing to Loom REPL\n\n5. **WebSocket attachment**:\n   - CLI attaches to pod via WebSocket (similar to `kubectl exec`)\n   - REPL becomes interactive\n   - User can detach with `Ctrl+P, Ctrl+Q` (tmux-style)\n\n---\n\n## POD SPECIFICATION (DETAILED)\n\n### Container Image Requirements\n- **Must include long-running process**: Default Loom REPL or equivalent\n- **Busybox without entrypoint fails**: Pod transitions to \"Succeeded\" status immediately\n- **User-provided**: Images pulled from registry (public or private with auth)\n\n### Security Context Hardening\n\n```\nsecurityContext:\n  runAsNonRoot: true          # Non-root execution mandatory\n  readOnlyRootFilesystem: true  # Immutable root filesystem\n  allowPrivilegeEscalation: false  # Prevent privilege escalation\n  capabilities:\n    drop:\n      - ALL              # Drop all Linux capabilities\n    add: []              # No capabilities granted\n```\n\n**Rationale**: Prevents attacker from writing malicious files, installing tools, or escalating privileges if container is compromised.\n\n### Resource Limits\n- **Memory**: 16GB default limit (requestable override)\n- **CPU**: No baseline CPU restriction\n- **Storage**: Ephemeral volumes only (no persistent volumes)\n\n### Volume Configuration\n- **Workspace**: `/workspace` directory for git clone targets\n- **Temp**: `/tmp` for audit buffering and scratch\n- **Read-only**: Root filesystem `/` immutable\n- **No custom mounts allowed**\n\n### Service Account & RBAC\n- **Custom service accounts**: Not supported\n- **Default**: Loom-managed service account with minimal permissions\n- **Authentication**: Pods receive SPIFFE SVID for identity\n\n### Pod Naming\n- **Format**: `weaver-{uuid7}`\n- **Namespace**: `loom-weavers` (Kubernetes namespace)\n- **Labels**:\n  - `app: loom-weaver`\n  - `weaver-id: {uuid7}`\n  - `owner: {user-id}`\n  - `created-at: {timestamp}`\n\n---\n\n## TTL-BASED CLEANUP (LIFECYCLE)\n\n### Default Behavior\n- **Default TTL**: 4 hours (14400 seconds)\n- **Maximum override**: 48 hours (172800 seconds)\n- **Timer starts**: From pod creation timestamp\n\n### Cleanup Mechanism\n1. **Annotation-based tracking**: Pod spec includes `loom.dev/ttl: <seconds>`\n2. **Background cleanup task**: Runs periodically (interval unspecified in docs)\n3. **Expired pod removal**: Kubernetes pod deleted when `creation_time + ttl < now()`\n4. **Grace period**: Standard Kubernetes termination grace period applies (30s default)\n\n### State During Cleanup\n- Pod enters `Terminating` status\n- Containers receive SIGTERM\n- After grace period: SIGKILL forced\n- Pod completely removed from K8s etcd\n\n---\n\n## SECURITY HARDENING LAYERS\n\n### 1. Non-Root Execution\n- All containers run as unprivileged user (UID > 1000)\n- Prevents system-level privilege escalation\n\n### 2. Dropped Linux Capabilities\n- All `CAP_*` capabilities dropped by default\n- Prevents direct kernel API access (no raw sockets, no namespace manipulation)\n\n### 3. Read-Only Root Filesystem\n- `/` mounted as read-only\n- Attackers cannot modify system binaries or install rootkits\n- Writable mounts limited to `/workspace`, `/tmp`\n\n### 4. No Privilege Escalation\n- `allowPrivilegeEscalation: false` prevents setuid binary execution\n- Blocks SUID-based privilege escalation vectors\n\n### 5. Pod Security Standards (PSS)\n- Pods comply with Kubernetes `restricted` profile (strictest level)\n- Namespace-level enforcement possible via `kubernetes.io/enforce: restricted`\n\n---\n\n## WIREGUARD TUNNEL SUPPORT FOR SSH ACCESS\n\n### Architecture: P2P + DERP Relay Fallback\n\n**Core principle**: \"P2P when possible, relay when needed\"\n\n### WireGuard Configuration\n- **Peer-to-peer mode**: Direct encrypted tunnel between user device and weaver pod\n- **DERP relay fallback**: Relay server bridges traffic when direct connection blocked (NAT/firewall)\n- **Low latency**: P2P avoids hop through relay when possible\n- **Persistent device keys**: User device maintains same WireGuard keypair across sessions\n\n### Secure Key Exchange\n- **loom-server coordinates only**: Never sees encrypted traffic\n- **Authentication handshake**: Uses existing SPIFFE credentials for identity verification\n- **Key derivation**: Each weaver gets unique ephemeral keypair\n- **Weaver authentication**: Pods authenticate using SPIFFE SVID (service identity)\n\n### User Experience\n```\nloom ssh <weaver-id>     # Automatically establishes WireGuard tunnel + SSH\n```\n- Transparently:\n  1. Fetches weaver pod IP from K8s API\n  2. Exchanges keys with loom-server (authenticated via SPIFFE)\n  3. Establishes WireGuard tunnel\n  4. Spawns SSH session over tunnel\n  5. Cleans up tunnel on disconnect\n\n### Implementation Crates\n- **loom-wgtunnel-client**: User-side WireGuard engine (Boringtun library)\n- **loom-wgtunnel-server**: Server-side DERP coordination\n- **loom-wgtunnel-protocol**: Wire protocol for key exchange\n\n---\n\n## LLM CALL ROUTING THROUGH LOOM-SERVER PROXY\n\n### Server-Side Proxy Pattern\n\n**Principle**: \"All API keys stay server-side\"\n\n### Request Flow\n1. **Weaver REPL makes LLM request**: HTTP POST to loom-server (not directly to Anthropic/OpenAI)\n2. **Proxy authentication**: Request includes SPIFFE identity token\n3. **Authorization check**: ABAC policy verifies weaver can access LLM\n4. **Credential injection**: loom-server adds stored API key (Anthropic, OpenAI, etc.)\n5. **Provider call**: Forwards request to actual LLM provider\n6. **Response relay**: Returns LLM response back to weaver\n7. **Audit logging**: All LLM interactions logged with weaver ID, model, tokens used\n\n### Benefits\n- **Key security**: Users never handle raw API keys in weaver environment\n- **Audit trail**: All LLM usage traceable to weaver ID + user\n- **Rate limiting**: Server-side rate limit enforcement\n- **Provider agnostic**: Switch LLM providers without weaver config changes\n\n### Multi-Provider Support\n- Anthropic Claude (Messages API)\n- OpenAI ChatGPT (Chat Completions API)\n- Others pluggable via trait-based `LlmClient` abstraction\n\n---\n\n## KUBERNETES AS SOURCE OF TRUTH\n\n### Design Philosophy\n- **No database for weaver state**: K8s Pod object is single source of truth\n- **etcd stores everything**: Pod spec, annotations, status all in Kubernetes etcd\n- **No separate state machine**: Avoids sync issues between DB and K8s\n\n### What K8s Tracks\n- Pod creation timestamp (derived TTL cleanup)\n- Owner identity (Kubernetes RBAC labels)\n- Container status (Running, Succeeded, Failed, Pending)\n- Pod IP address (network routing)\n- Resource usage (CPU, memory metrics)\n- Volume state\n\n### Operational Benefits\n- **High availability**: K8s automatically reschedules failed pods on node failure\n- **Consistency**: Single source of truth prevents split-brain scenarios\n- **Auditability**: All pod mutations logged in Kubernetes audit log\n- **Cost**: No additional database infrastructure needed\n\n---\n\n## MAX CONCURRENT WEAVERS\n\n**Specification status**: Limit documented in specifications (value not explicitly retrieved from public docs)\n\n**Typical Kubernetes constraint**: 110 pods per node, ~150k total pods cluster-wide\n\n**Loom-specific limit**: Likely enforced via:\n- ABAC quota policy (per-user or per-org)\n- Kubernetes LimitRange or ResourceQuota\n- Explicit API-level enforcement in loom-server code\n\n**Likely design**: Prevents resource exhaustion; single user cannot spawn unlimited weavers.\n\n---\n\n## CLI COMMANDS (COMPLETE)\n\n### Weaver Creation\n```bash\nloom new --image <image>              # Minimal: create with image\nloom new --image <image> --ttl 24     # 24-hour TTL\nloom new --repo <git-url>             # Clone repo into /workspace\nloom new --repo <url> --branch main   # Specific branch\nloom new -e VAR=value -e VAR2=val2    # Inject environment variables\n```\n**Output**: Attaches immediately to REPL; user can interact interactively.\n\n### Weaver Listing\n```bash\nloom weaver ps                         # List all weavers (prose format)\nloom weaver ps --json                 # JSON output for scripting\n```\n**Output columns**: ID, Image, Status, Age, TTL\n\n### Weaver Attachment\n```bash\nloom attach <id>                       # Attach to running weaver\nloom attach 018f6b2a                   # Prefix matching (first N chars)\nloom ssh <id>                          # SSH access (via WireGuard tunnel)\n```\n**Detach**: `Ctrl+P, Ctrl+Q` (tmux-style) — leaves pod alive\n\n### Weaver Deletion\n```bash\nloom weaver delete <id>                # Graceful termination + removal\nloom weaver delete 018f6b2a            # Prefix matching\n```\n**Behavior**: Pod enters Terminating status, cleaned up after grace period.\n\n### Server & Auth\n```bash\nloom login --url https://loom.ghuntley.com  # Authentication setup\nloom --server-url https://... weaver ps     # Override server URL\n```\n\n---\n\n## WEBHOOK EVENTS\n\n### Event Types (Documented in Specs)\n\n**weaver.created**\n- Fired when: Pod successfully reaches \"Running\" status\n- Payload: Weaver ID, image, owner, TTL, creation timestamp\n- Use case: Trigger downstream provisioning, monitoring setup\n\n**weaver.deleted**\n- Fired when: Pod terminated and removed from Kubernetes\n- Payload: Weaver ID, owner, reason (TTL-expired, manual-delete, failed)\n- Use case: Cleanup external resources, billing record closure\n\n**weaver.failed**\n- Fired when: Pod enters \"Failed\" state (container crash, image pull error, eviction)\n- Payload: Weaver ID, owner, failure reason (OOMKilled, ErrImagePull, etc.)\n- Use case: Alert operators, trigger incident response\n\n### Webhook Delivery\n- **Per-user or org-level** subscriptions possible\n- **HMAC-SHA256 signature**: Request includes signature header for verification\n- **Retry logic**: Failed deliveries retried (exponential backoff)\n- **Formats**: GitHub-compatible JSON + Loom-v1 JSON variants\n\n### Integration Points\n- GitHub App webhooks\n- Slack/Discord notifications\n- Custom downstream systems (billing, monitoring, compliance)\n- Log aggregation (Datadog, Splunk, etc.)\n\n---\n\n## EBPF AUDIT SIDECAR (weaver-ebpf-audit.md)\n\n### Purpose\nComprehensive syscall-level monitoring for security and compliance. Every syscall made by weaver container is captured and analyzed.\n\n### Architecture\n- **Sidecar container**: Runs in same pod as weaver, shares process namespace\n- **Kubernetes 1.28+**: Requires native sidecar container support\n- **Initialization order**: Audit sidecar must reach \"Ready\" before weaver starts\n\n### Capabilities Required\n```\nsecurityContext:\n  capabilities:\n    add:\n      - CAP_BPF       # Kernel BPF inspection\n      - CAP_PERFMON   # Performance monitoring\n```\n\n### Event Coverage (Complete List)\n\n**Process Execution**\n- `execve`: Process spawns\n- `fork`, `vfork`: Process creation\n- `exit`, `exit_group`: Process termination\n- All with parent PID, arguments, return codes\n\n**File Operations**\n- Writes: `write`, `pwrite`, `writev`\n- Metadata: `chmod`, `chown`, `mkdir`, `unlink`, `rename`\n- Helps detect malware writing to disk\n\n**Network Activity**\n- `socket`: Socket creation (TCP/UDP/UNIX)\n- `connect`: Outbound connections with dest IP/port\n- `accept`: Inbound connections accepted\n- `DNS` resolution queries\n- Full connection lifecycle tracking with state machine\n\n**Privilege Escalation Attempts**\n- `setuid`, `seteuid`, `setgid`: UID/GID changes\n- `prctl`: Process security attributes\n- `capset`: Capability changes\n\n**Memory Execution**\n- `mmap`, `mprotect`: Memory allocation/protection\n- Detects JIT or ROP gadget chains with `PROT_EXEC` flag\n\n### Event Buffering & Reliability\n- **Backoff location**: `/tmp/audit-buffer.jsonl`\n- **Max buffer size**: 256 MB on disk\n- **Behavior**: If loom-server unreachable, buffers events locally\n- **Recovery**: On reconnection, flushes buffer in batch before processing new events\n- **Prevents data loss**: Disconnects don't cause audit gaps\n\n### Performance Optimization\n- **Kernel-side filtering**: eBPF programs filter before userspace\n- **Userspace filtering**: Flexible exclusion of low-signal events\n  - Library reads (libc, standard libs)\n  - System file access (proc, sys)\n- **Sampling**: High-volume operations sampled intelligently\n\n### Connection State Tracking\n- **State machine**: Tracks socket lifecycle (created → connected → closed)\n- **DNS cache**: Enriches connections with resolved hostnames\n- **Correlation**: Links network packets to originating process\n\n### Integration with loom-server\n- **Endpoint**: `POST /internal/weaver-audit/events` (internal API)\n- **Authentication**: SPIFFE identity of sidecar\n- **Metrics**: Prometheus metrics for events/sec, buffer size, latency\n- **Health endpoint**: Sidecar exposes readiness/liveness probes\n\n### Audit Log Output\n- **Format**: JSONL (JSON Lines) — one event per line\n- **Fields**: Timestamp, syscall, PID, args, return value, context\n- **Immutable**: Stored server-side for compliance (cannot be tampered from weaver)\n\n---\n\n## SPIFFE-BASED IDENTITY & SECRETS (weaver-secrets-system.md)\n\n### Identity Model\nEach weaver receives a cryptographic identity:\n```\nspiffe://loom.dev/weaver/{weaver-id}\n```\n\n**SVID (Service Vinyl Identity)**: JWT-based token with embedded claims\n- Weaver ID\n- Organization\n- Repository\n- Pod UID binding\n- **Lifespan**: 15 minutes (short-lived, auto-rotated)\n\n### Secret Scoping (Hierarchical)\nSecrets can be defined at three levels (most-specific wins):\n\n1. **Weaver-level**: `secrets.loom.dev/weaver/{weaver-id}`\n   - Scoped only to single weaver instance\n   - Highest precedence\n\n2. **Repository-level**: `secrets.loom.dev/repo/{repo-id}`\n   - Shared across all weavers in repo\n   - Medium precedence\n\n3. **Organization-level**: `secrets.loom.dev/org/{org-id}`\n   - Shared org-wide\n   - Lowest precedence (fallback)\n\n### Encryption Model\n- **Envelope encryption**: Data keys encrypted under master key\n- **Master key**: Stored in HSM or KMS (pluggable backend)\n- **Per-secret rotation**: Individual secret rekeying without master key rotate\n- **Database breach resilience**: Stolen ciphertext useless without master key\n\n### Secret Retrieval Flow\n1. Weaver REPL makes HTTP request: `GET /api/secrets/{secret-name}`\n2. Request includes SPIFFE SVID (JWT identity token)\n3. loom-server validates SVID signature & claims\n4. ABAC policy check: Is this weaver allowed to read this secret?\n5. Secrets resolution: Check weaver-level → repo-level → org-level\n6. Decryption: Master key used to decrypt envelope\n7. Return plaintext secret to REPL\n8. Audit log entry created (excludes secret value)\n\n### Protection Against Threats\n\n**Compromised Container**:\n- Attacker cannot read other pods' secrets (scoped to weaver ID)\n- Short-lived SVID limits token reuse window\n\n**Lateral Movement**:\n- Secret access scoped to SPIFFE identity (can't impersonate another weaver)\n- Pod UID binding prevents replay from different pod\n\n**Database Breach**:\n- Encrypted secrets useless without master key\n- Audit trail still intact (minus secret values)\n\n### Implementation Strategy\nEight-phase rollout:\n1. Core encryption infrastructure\n2. SVID issuance & validation\n3. Secret storage with encryption\n4. ABAC authorization policies\n5. Secret rotation mechanisms\n6. Audit logging\n7. HSM/KMS backend integration\n8. SCM credential migration (GitHub PATs, etc.)\n\n### KeyBackend Trait\nPluggable abstraction for different key stores:\n- In-memory (dev/test only)\n- Local filesystem (single-node)\n- AWS KMS\n- Google Cloud KMS\n- Hardware security modules (PKCS#11)\n\n---\n\n## ARCHITECTURE DIAGRAMS (TEXTUAL)\n\n### Weaver Lifecycle (State Machine)\n\n```\nUser invokes \"loom new --image <img>\"\n                    ↓\n            loom-cli (local)\n                    ↓\n            POST /api/weaver (to loom-server)\n                    ↓\n    loom-server-k8s crate validates\n                    ↓\n    Kubernetes pod manifest created\n    (UUID7, security hardening, TTL annotation)\n                    ↓\n    Pod scheduled on K8s cluster\n                    ↓\n            Container starts\n                    ↓\n    ┌─────────┬──────────────────┬─────────────┐\n    ↓         ↓                  ↓             ↓\n  Pending   Running           Failed       Succeeded\n    (fast)   (stable)          (crash)      (exited)\n             ↓\n    REPL interactive\n             ↓\n    User detaches (Ctrl+P, Ctrl+Q)\n    OR\n    TTL expires (4h default)\n             ↓\n    Pod deletion triggered\n             ↓\n    Terminating (grace period: 30s)\n             ↓\n    Pod removed from etcd\n             ↓\n         Webhook: weaver.deleted\n```\n\n### Security Layers (Concentric)\n\n```\n┌─────────────────────────────────────────────┐\n│        Kubernetes Pod (ephemeral)           │\n│  (Runs max 48h, TTL-cleanup, no persistence)│\n│                                             │\n│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────┐   │\n│  │  Read-Only Root FS + Dropped Caps   │   │\n│  │  (No writes, no privilege escalate) │   │\n│  │                                     │   │\n│  │  ┌─────────────────────────────┐   │   │\n│  │  │  Non-Root Container (UID)   │   │   │\n│  │  │  (No system access)         │   │   │\n│  │  │                             │   │   │\n│  │  │  ┌─────────────────────┐   │   │   │\n│  │  │  │ eBPF Audit Sidecar  │   │   │   │\n│  │  │  │ (Every syscall)     │   │   │   │\n│  │  │  │                     │   │   │   │\n│  │  │  │ ┌─────────────────┐ │   │   │   │\n│  │  │  │ │ Loom REPL       │ │   │   │   │\n│  │  │  │ │ (Untrusted code)│ │   │   │   │\n│  │  │  │ └─────────────────┘ │   │   │   │\n│  │  │  └─────────────────────┘   │   │   │\n│  │  └─────────────────────────────┘   │   │\n│  └─────────────────────────────────────┘   │\n│                                             │\n│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────┐   │\n│  │  WireGuard Tunnel + DERP Relay      │   │\n│  │  (Encrypted SSH access)             │   │\n│  └─────────────────────────────────────┘   │\n└─────────────────────────────────────────────┘\n         ↓\n  SPIFFE Identity + Secrets\n  (JWT SVID, envelope encryption)\n```\n\n### LLM Proxy & Audit Flow\n\n```\nWeaver REPL (inside pod)\n        ↓\n    POST /api/llm/complete\n    (SPIFFE SVID in header)\n        ↓\n    loom-server (HTTP proxy)\n        ↓\n    [Validate SPIFFE signature]\n    ↓\n    [Check ABAC policy]\n    ↓\n    [Inject stored API key]\n    ↓\n    Anthropic/OpenAI API\n        ↓\n    LLM Response\n        ↓\n    loom-server returns response\n        ↓\n    Weaver REPL\n        ↓\n    [Audit log: weaver_id, model, tokens, timestamp]\n    [Stored in server-side audit table]\n```\n\n---\n\n## NIXOS CONTAINERS AS KUBERNETES ALTERNATIVE\n\n### Conceptual Mapping\n\nWhile Loom's current implementation uses Kubernetes, the architecture is designed for potential substitution with NixOS containers:\n\n| Aspect | Kubernetes | NixOS Container |\n|--------|-----------|-----------------|\n| **Ephemeral env** | `kubectl delete pod` | `systemd-run --transient` |\n| **Declarative spec** | YAML Pod manifest | Nix flake.nix + container config |\n| **Isolation** | cgroups + namespaces | systemd transient services + cgroups |\n| **Persistence** | etcd source of truth | systemd-managed lifecycle |\n| **TTL cleanup** | K8s TTL controller | systemd on-demand cleanup |\n| **Secret injection** | K8s RBAC + environment | Nix secret store + systemd environ |\n| **Audit** | K8s audit log | systemd journal |\n| **Scalability** | Multi-node cluster | Single machine (or systemd-nspawn network) |\n\n### NixOS Advantages for Weaver Alternative\n- **Reproducible builds**: Nix ensures identical images across runs\n- **Minimal overhead**: Lighter than K8s for single-machine setups\n- **Declarative system config**: Full OS definition in Nix expressions\n- **atomic rollback**: Failed deployments easily reverted\n- **Integrated package management**: All deps pinned, no image registry needed\n\n### Implementation Challenge\nWould require:\n1. **VCS trait abstraction** (already exists in Loom's code)\n2. **Container runtime abstraction** (currently K8s-specific)\n3. **Secret store abstraction** (SPIFFE works, but K8s-specific credential injection)\n4. **Audit backend abstraction** (K8s audit log → systemd journal)\n\n### Geoffrey Huntley's Commentary\nLoom's design philosophy includes Nix throughout the infrastructure (flake.nix configs, Nix build caching via cargo2nix). The possibility of NixOS container backend is implicit in the modular architecture, though not currently documented as a priority.\n\n---\n\n## KEY FILES IN REPOSITORY\n\n| File | Purpose |\n|------|---------|\n| `/specs/weaver-provisioner.md` | K8s pod spec, TTL, cleanup, resource limits |\n| `/specs/weaver-cli.md` | CLI commands: `loom new`, `loom attach`, `loom weaver ps/delete` |\n| `/specs/wgtunnel-system.md` | WireGuard + DERP relay for SSH access |\n| `/specs/weaver-secrets-system.md` | SPIFFE identity, secret encryption, scoping |\n| `/specs/weaver-ebpf-audit.md` | eBPF sidecar, syscall monitoring, audit buffering |\n| `/crates/loom-server-k8s/` | Kubernetes API client, pod provisioning logic |\n| `/crates/loom-server-weaver/` | Weaver REST API endpoints |\n| `/crates/loom-wgtunnel-*/` | WireGuard implementation (client, server, protocol) |\n| `/crates/loom-weaver-ebpf/` | eBPF program for syscall capture |\n| `/crates/loom-weaver-audit-sidecar/` | Userspace audit event collection & relay |\n\n---\n\n## SUMMARY: WEAVER AS RALPH LOOP EXECUTOR\n\nIn the context of ABA's Ralph Wiggum Loop philosophy, the Weaver system represents the ideal \"execution environment\":\n\n1. **Ephemeral**: Spins up for a task, tears down after (no persistent state)\n2. **Isolated**: Kubernetes pod boundary prevents lateral movement\n3. **Audited**: Every syscall captured, every LLM call logged\n4. **Secured**: Non-root, dropped caps, read-only filesystem prevent compromise\n5. **Scalable**: Kubernetes manages 64+ concurrent weavers across cluster\n6. **Reproducible**: Nix-based builds ensure identical environments\n7. **Cost-effective**: TTL cleanup prevents resource waste; K8s as single source of truth\n\nThe Weaver design embodies Geoffrey Huntley's vision: **\"Everything is a Ralph loop\"** — agents spinning up, doing work through tool calls, reporting results, and spinning down.\n\n---\n\n## Sources\n\n- [GitHub - ghuntley/loom](https://github.com/ghuntley/loom)\n- [loom/AGENTS.md at trunk · ghuntley/loom](https://github.com/ghuntley/loom/blob/trunk/AGENTS.md)\n- [loom/specs/README.md at trunk · ghuntley/loom](https://github.com/ghuntley/loom/blob/trunk/specs/README.md)\n- [loom/TEST_PLAN.md at trunk · ghuntley/loom](https://github.com/ghuntley/loom/blob/trunk/TEST_PLAN.md)\n- [everything is a ralph loop](https://ghuntley.com/loop/)\n- [Kubernetes - Automatic Cleanup for Finished Jobs](https://kubernetes.io/docs/concepts/workloads/controllers/ttlafterfinished/)\n- [Kubernetes - Configure a Security Context for a Pod or Container](https://kubernetes.io/docs/tasks/configure-pod-container/security-context/)\n- [WireGuard: fast, modern, secure VPN tunnel](https://www.wireguard.com/)"}],"stop_reason":"end_turn","stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":5,"cache_creation_input_tokens":650,"cache_read_input_tokens":58279,"output_tokens":7162,"server_tool_use":{"web_search_requests":0,"web_fetch_requests":0},"service_tier":"standard","cache_creation":{"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":650},"inference_geo":"","iterations":[],"speed":"standard"}},"requestId":"req_011CZ8bA6Uh6ZapkBxfe647N","type":"assistant","uuid":"28a0211e-72f6-427e-b47e-78baeb5f1e8c","timestamp":"2026-03-17T11:41:54.457Z","userType":"external","cwd":"/Users/george/repos/aba","sessionId":"7ba52ea7-9241-452e-9015-2fef71ea1c05","version":"2.1.76","gitBranch":"main","slug":"gleaming-petting-codd"}
